353 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Longines-Wittnauer Watch Co. v. Barnes & Reinecke, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 443; 209 N.E.2d 68; 261 N.Y.S.2d 8; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1319; 24 A.L.R.3d 508


January 7, 1965, Argued  
May 27, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: In Longines-Wittnauer: Order affirmed, with costs. Question certified answered in the affirmative.

In Feathers v. McLucas: Order of Appellate Division reversed and that of Special Term reinstated, with costs in this court and in the Appellate Division. Question certified answered in the negative.

In Singer v. Walker: Order affirmed, with costs. Question certified answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three separate actions, one sounding in contract and two in tort, appellant foreign corporations challenged decisions of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in both the First Judicial Department and Third Judicial Department (New York), which determined that personal jurisdiction existed over appellants under the long arm statute, N.Y. C.P.L.R. 302.


OVERVIEW: In three cases under review, one sounding in contract and two in tort, the court was called upon to decide whether lower courts had acquired personal jurisdiction over appellant foreign corporations under the long arm statute, N.Y. C.P.L.R. 302. The court found that in the first action there was jurisdiction under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 302(a)(1) because appellant had transacted business in the state where there were substantial preliminary negotiations, actual execution of the supplementary contract took place in the state, and services were rendered in the state. The court found that in the second action appellant was not subject to jurisdiction under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 302(a)(2) because appellant did not commit a tortious act within the state. The court found that in the third action there was no jurisdiction on the ground that appellant committed a tortious act within the state, but jurisdiction existed on the ground that appellant transacted business within the state. In two of the three actions, the orders of the lower courts were affirmed and the certified questions answered in the affirmative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions in two of the three actions, holding that personal jurisdiction existed under the long arm statute over appellant foreign corporations transacting business within the state. The court reversed the decision in a third action, holding that there was no jurisdiction over appellant foreign corporation that did not commit a tortious act within the state.


HEADNOTES

Process -- service on nonresidents -- "long-arm" statute ( CPLR 302) is procedural in nature and embraces suits commenced after its effective date based on previously accrued causes of action -- in action for damages for breach of warranty in connection with manufacture and sale of machines, foreign manufacturer's activities within state constituted "[transaction of] any business within the state" within CPLR 302 so as to give New York courts jurisdiction of manufacturer by service of process on it within foreign state -- in second action to recover damages for personal injuries and property damage resulting from explosion of tractor-drawn steel tank, jurisdiction was not obtained of foreign manufacturer of tank by service of process on it in foreign state since its improper assemblage of tank was "tortious act" not committed "within" state -- in third action to recover damages sustained when geologist's hammer manufactured and labeled without state broke, jurisdiction of foreign manufacturer cannot be sustained on basis of "tortious act" committed "within" state -- but can be sustained on basis that manufacturer transacted business within state.

1. The "long-arm" statute ( CPLR 302) which, effective September 1, 1963, granted jurisdiction to New York courts over a nondomiciliary who "transacts any business within the state" or "commits a tortious act within the state" embraces suits instituted after its effective date but based on previously accrued causes of action. Section 302 is of a procedural and remedial nature and thus applicable to actions thereafter instituted for the redress of wrongs already done. It does not create new rights but merely facilitates the enforcement locally of pre-existing rights. Moreover, CPLR 10003 states that the CPLR "shall apply to all actions hereafter commenced" whether based on previously or subsequently accrued causes of action. The retroactive application of CPLR 302 is constitutionally valid.

2. In an action for damages for breach of warranty in the manufacture and sale of machines by a foreign corporation having its place of business in Chicago, personal jurisdiction of defendant was properly acquired by service upon it of a summons and complaint in Illinois, where defendant's activities within this State in connection with the sale included substantial preliminary negotiations through high-level personnel during a period of some two months; the actual execution of a supplementary contract; the shipment for use here, subject to acceptance following delivery, of two specially designed machines, priced at $ 118,000, and the rendition of services over a period of some three months by two of defendant's top engineers in supervising the installation and testing of the complex machines. Defendant's contacts with this State were such that the maintenance of the action does not offend traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice.

3. In a second action to recover damages for personal injuries and property damage resulting from the explosion in New York of a tractor-drawn steel tank manufactured in Kansas by a Kansas corporation, sold to a Missouri corporation which mounted it on a wheelbase and then in turn sold to a licensed interstate carrier in Pennsylvania whose agents were driving its tractor in this State when the tank exploded, personal jurisdiction was not obtained, pursuant to CPLR 302 (subd. [a], par. 2), of the Kansas corporation by service of a summons and complaint upon it in Kansas. The Kansas corporation never transacted business in New York, and the tortious act charged against it -- that it improperly designed and assembled the tank -- occurred in Kansas. The language of paragraph 2 conferring personal jurisdiction over a nondomiciliary if he "commits a tortious act within the state" cannot be read as synonymous with "commits a tortious act without the state which causes injury within the state". The occurrence of the injury in this State cannot serve to transmute an out-of-state tortious act into one committed here within the sense of the statutory wording. ( Gray v. American Radiator & Sanitary Corp., 22 Ill. 2d 432, not followed.)

4. In a third action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained when a geologist's hammer manufactured in Illinois by an Illinois corporation which marked it "unbreakable", and purchased for infant plaintiff in New York, broke in Connecticut, and damaged infant plaintiff's eye, personal jurisdiction of the manufacturer on the ground that it committed a tortious act within the State within CPLR 302 (subd. [a], par. 2) cannot be sustained. The tortious acts of manufacturing and labeling the hammer occurred in Illinois and are insufficient to satisfy the requirement of paragraph 2 that the "tortious act" be one committed "within" this State. That a product defectively manufactured and misleadingly labeled in one state is marketed and sold in another cannot serve to change the place where the original tortious acts were committed or to create a new tortious act.

5. Jurisdiction of the Illinois manufacturer, however, can be sustained on the ground that it "[transacted] * * * business within the state" ( CPLR 302, subd. [a], par. 1) and that the pleaded cause of action is one "arising" therefrom. Paragraph 1 is not limited to actions in contract and applies to tort actions when supported by a sufficient showing of facts. Defendant shipped substantial quantities of its products into this State as the result of solicitation here through a local manufacturer's representative and through catalogues and advertisements and the injury-causing hammer, purchased from a New York dealer, was one of such products. Defendant's activities in this State are sufficient to satisfy the statutory criterion of transaction of business as well as the constitutional requirement of minimum contacts. It is not determinative that the formal execution of its sales contracts may have occurred in Illinois rather than New York. Nor is it a controlling consideration that the actual injury happened to take place in Connecticut, since the cause of action asserted is clearly one "arising from" the purposeful activities engaged in by defendant in this State in connection with the sale of its products in the New York market.

 

354 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re City of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


16 N.Y.2d 497; 208 N.E.2d 172; 260 N.Y.S.2d 439; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1409


November 24, 1964, Argued  
April 22, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs, in a memorandum.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city challenged an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which modified, and, as modified, affirmed, certain portions of the fifth and sixth separate and partial final decrees of the special term making awards in proceedings to acquire title to real property required for the Lincoln Square Slum Clearance Project of the City of New York.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimants challenged the judgment of the appellate division affirming an order of the special term denying a motion by the claimants for an order directing that, in lieu of a four percent interest allowance upon the awards made to them, there should be added, to fee awards, a sum equal to the annual net rental value of each fee parcel and, to fixture awards, a sum equal to six percent of each award. The court affirmed the orders. The court held as follows: (1) an award of costs to a successful appellant was governed by N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 8107, which was not an unconstitutional diminution of the award; (2) the rate of interest to be paid upon any judgment or accrued claim against a municipal corporation arising out of a condemnation proceeding was not to exceed four per centum per annum pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law, §3-a; and (3) the awards were properly supported by proof bearing on market value taken together with the actual rents on the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the appellate division.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- compensation -- Appellate Division reduced various awards made by Special Term for parcels taken by City of New York for Lincoln Square Slum Clearance Project, and affirmed order of Special Term denying motion by certain claimants concerning interest upon awards -- contentions by various claimants that reductions were result of application of erroneous principles of law and were not supported by record, that assessment of costs against claimant in condemnation proceeding was unconstitutional, that quantum of damages for delay in payment of awards could not, constitutionally, be limited by statute, and that denial of opportunity to offer proof as to normal commercial rate of interest constituted denial of claimants' constitutional rights -- order of Appellate Division affirmed -- rate of interest to be paid upon judgment or accrued claim against municipal corporation arising out of condemnation proceeding" shall not exceed four per centum per annum" (General Municipal Law, § 3-a) -- award of costs to successful appellant is governed by CPLR 8107, which Court of Appeals does not regard as unconstitutional diminution of award -- as to certain damage parcels, reductions were supported by fair preponderance of evidence -- inadvertent error committed by Appellate Division does not require reversal since it took proper principle into consideration along with other proof which supported reduced awards. 

 

355 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Miles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 364; 207 N.E.2d 181; 259 N.Y.S.2d 129; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1439


February 3, 1965, Argued  
April 15, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, with costs in this court and in the Appellate Division, and matter remitted to the Appellate Division for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed an order from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which entered judgment finding that defendants did not have any interest in the subject property because they failed to record their intent and declaration of reversionary interest in accordance with N.Y. Real Prop. Law § 345.


OVERVIEW: Judgment finding that defendants were not vested with any reversionary right to reenter property where the condition requiring it to be used as a school facility was breached was reversed. The lower court found that because the intent and declaration of reversionary interest was not recorded in accordance with N.Y. Real Prop. Law § 345, defendant's right to renter the property was extinguished. On appeal, the court found that the statute as applied was unconstitutional. According to the court, § 345 was unconstitutional as impairing the obligation of the contract contained in the deed, and depriving the reversioner of its property without due process of law. The court concluded that under the circumstances, § 345 could not be sustained since it purported to bar the remedy before the right to enforce it had matured. Hence, the court determined that defendants had the right to reenter the property upon the breach of the contract provision prohibiting any use of the property other than for school purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in plaintiffs' favor and entered judgment finding that defendants had the right to reenter the property upon breach of the conditions of the deed. The court held that the statute requiring recordation of the intent and declaration of reversionary interest was unconstitutional because it denied defendants of their property without due process.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- rights of reverter -- Real Property Law ( § 345, subd. 4), insofar as it purports to extinguish rights of reverter unless owners of such rights shall record declarations of intent to preserve their rights before September 1, 1961, is unconstitutional and void as applied to reverter which did not mature until 1962 under 1854 deed which provided for reverter to grantor or his heirs if premises were no longer used for educational purposes -- grantor's heirs and devisees are entitled to judgment declaring that they are now vested with fee title.

Defendants' ancestor conveyed a parcel of land to plaintiff's predecessor by a deed which was recorded in 1854 and which stated: "Provided nevertheless that the said lot and the building thereon shall be used for the purposes of an Academy and no other then this deed shall remain in full force and effect otherwise it shall become Void and the premises herein conveyed shall revert to the said John Townsend party of the first part and to his heirs." The land was used for educational purposes until April 1, 1962, when such use was discontinued. Section 345 of the Real Property Law was enacted by chapter 865 of the Laws of 1958. This statute states that conditions subsequent or special limitations restricting the use of land, and the rights of reverter created thereby, shall be extinguished unless the owners of such rights of reverter shall record declarations of intent to preserve their rights; and, if such condition subsequent or special limitation was created before September 1, 1931, such declaration must be recorded on or before September 1, 1961 (Real Property Law, § 345, subd. 4). But a right of reverter is a property right. In 1961 this land was still being used for educational purposes and the reversion would not mature or take effect in enjoyment until some indefinite future time. As thus applied, this portion of subdivision 4 of section 345 is not a valid Statute of Limitations, since it purports to bar the remedy before the right of enforcement has matured; nor is it a valid recording act designed to protect innocent third-party purchasers for value, since it bars a property right as between the parties or their successors. This portion of subdivision 4 of section 345 of the Real Property Law is unconstitutional, since it impairs the obligation of contract and deprives the owners of their property without due process of law. The defendants are entitled to judgment declaring that they are vested with title in fee to the property, free from any claim of plaintiff thereto.

358 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Orans


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 339; 206 N.E.2d 854; 258 N.Y.S.2d 825; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1492


March 30, 1965, Argued  
April 14, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state officers sought review of the order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which held the reapportionment statutes, 1964 N.Y. Laws 976, 977, 978, 979, 981, violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 2 because they called for an assembly of more than 150 members. Petitioner citizens cross-appealed from the portion of the order that held the statutes were not invalid by reason of their having been enacted at a special session.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted five reapportionment statutes during an extraordinary session. The trial court held the reapportionment statutes unconstitutional on the sole ground that they called for an assembly of more than 150 members. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the flat, positive, and unmistakable command in N.Y. Const. art. III, § 2 that there be 150 members of the state assembly was in full effect. Because each of the four plans violated that command, each plan and all five reapportionment statutes, 1964 N.Y. Laws 976, 977, 978, 979, 981, were invalid. The 150-member provision of N.Y. Const. art. III, § 2 was separate and severable from the elaborate and complex formulae that the highest federal court struck down as violating the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. There was no showing that the highest federal court's mandate for equally populated districts could not be obeyed if the assembly districts numbered exactly 150. The court held that passage of reapportionment statutes at a special session was not forbidden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which held that the reapportionment statutes violated the New York Constitution because they called for an assembly of more than 150 members and that the reapportionment statutes were not invalid on the ground that they were enacted at a special session.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- apportionment of Legislature -- statutes enacted at extraordinary session of Legislature which set up four plans for apportioning and districting State Senate and Assembly (L. 1964, chs. 976, 977, 978, 979, 981) are unconstitutional, since each establishes Assembly of more than 150 members and State Constitution (art. III, § 2) states that "The assembly shall consist of one hundred and fifty members."

1. Statutes which were enacted at an extraordinary session of the Legislature and set up four separate plans for apportioning and districting the State Senate and Assembly (L. 1964, chs. 976, 977, 978, 979, 981) are unconstitutional since each establishes an Assembly of more than 150 members, whereas the State Constitution (art. III, § 2) states that "The assembly shall consist of one hundred and fifty members."

2. Neither the United States Supreme Court nor the Federal District Court in the litigation which resulted in holding the New York Legislature to be invalidly organized determined that the limitation of 150 members was unconstitutional.

3. It is not and cannot be shown that the Supreme Court's mandate for equally populated districts could not be obeyed if the Assembly districts numbered 150.

4. The statutes were not invalid because passed at a special session of the Legislature and not at a regular session ( Matter of Reynolds, 202 N. Y. 430, 443-444).

5. The unconstitutionality found by the United States Supreme Court relates almost entirely to the second paragraph of section 5 and to the provision in the first paragraph that each county, no matter how small, shall have an Assembly member. There is no reason why the balance of section 5 should not be obeyed, especially its requirement that Assembly districts be "compact * * * convenient and contiguous", and including so far as possible all the other directions in the fourth paragraph of section 5.

6. Section 3 of article III of the State Constitution, insofar as it delimits the Senate districts, is completely void. Also, the apportionment and locating of Senate districts by the new statutes fall with the invalidated Assembly districting in the same statutes since the Constitution (art. III, § 5) provides that the apportionment of Assembly districts and Senate districts must be "by the same law".

7. The third paragraph of section 4 which permits the increase of State Senate districts above 50 is valid (see Matter of Fay, 291 N. Y. 198) except that it is subject to the requirement that districts must be substantially equal in population. The long full paragraph at the beginning seems still to be applicable except possibly the prohibitions in its last two sentences which should, however, be respected if it be mathematically possible so to do and still obey the "one man, one vote" basic rule.

8. The districting outlawed by the United States Supreme Court as well as all former districtings of this State use the county as the basic unit into which both Assembly and Senate districts are molded, but under the new rules the integrity of all the counties in these respects cannot be complete. Not only will it be impossible to give each county at least one full Assembly district but also the boundaries of districts cannot in all instances be co-terminal with county borders. Also, the fourth paragraph of section 5 of article III giving local legislatures the power to draw Assembly district lines in counties having more than one Assembly district cannot survive, since in some instances part of an Assembly district will have to be in one county and part in another.

9. The redistricting should not be left to the Federal courts. The Legislature is under an obligation to reapportion and the Federal courts intervene only as a last resort.

360 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Portelli


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 235; 205 N.E.2d 857; 257 N.Y.S.2d 931; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1538


January 14, 1965, Argued  
March 11, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which convicted defendants of the crime of murder in the first degree. Defendants contended that a witness's testimony regarding defendants' involvement in the crime should have been stricken once it appeared that his statement, although given some eight months before the trial, had been coerced by the police.


OVERVIEW: A witness testified at trial that defendants told him how they had killed the two police officers during a holdup. The witness's trial testimony was the same as a statement he had made to police eight months earlier. At trial, the witness declared that he made the statement to police only after he had been held in custody overnight and severely beaten and tortured and that he would not have talked to the police had they not coerced him in this manner. However, the witness insisted from the witness stand that the pretrial statement, which he made to the police, as well as his testimony, implicating defendants, was completely true. The court affirmed the convictions. The court found that while an out-of-court confession coerced from a defendant would be excluded from evidence, the testimony of a witness who, although previously forced to make a pretrial statement, asserted that his testimony at the trial was truthful, was for the consideration and appraisal of the jury. The requirements of law were met if the fact of such earlier coercion or other official lawlessness was disclosed to the jurors so that they could pass upon the witness's veracity and credibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- coercion of witness -- although, prior to trial, witness had been coerced by police into making statement implicating defendant, witness stated at trial that statement was true, and coercion was disclosed to jury -- testimony was admissible.

Although, prior to the trial, a witness against defendants had been coerced by the police into making a statement implicating defendant Portelli, the witness testified at the trial that the statement was true. In view of such testimony, and since the coercion was disclosed to the jury, the witness' trial testimony was admissible and its consideration was for the jury.

 

361 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Martinis v. Supreme Court


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 240; 206 N.E.2d 165; 258 N.Y.S.2d 65; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1539


December 1, 1964, Argued  
March 11, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, supreme court justices and others, sought review of an order by the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which prohibited the prosecution from trying petitioner on an indictment charging him with criminal negligence in the operation of an automobile resulting in the death of a human being and assault in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had a car accident that killed five people and seriously injured another person. He was charged with driving while in an intoxicated condition, reckless driving, leaving the scene of an accident without reporting damage to property, and without reporting injury to a person in violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law §§ 1192, 1190, 600. He was found not guilty of those offenses and the information was dismissed. Later, a grand jury returned an indictment charging petitioner with five separate counts of vehicular homicide under N.Y. Penal Law § 1053-a and one count of assault in the third degree under N.Y. Penal Law § 244. Petitioner filed a writ of prohibition contended that the second trial subjected him to double jeopardy. The trial court granted the writ and respondents sought review. On review, the court reversed the order because petitioner was not exposed to double jeopardy in the second trial. The court held that the new charges against petitioner were clearly independent and unrelated violations of different statutes for which a conviction could be had only on proof involving different elements and triable only in courts possessing appropriate jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order prohibiting petitioner's prosecution for vehicular homicide and dismissed the petition for writ of prohibition.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- double jeopardy -- in proceeding for order prohibiting trial of charge of vehicular homicide (Penal Law, § 1053-a) on ground that trial would subject petitioner to double jeopardy because he had previously been found not guilty of reckless driving (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 1190), petition dismissed.

In a proceeding for an order prohibiting the trial of petitioner on an indictment charging him with vehicular homicide (Penal Law, § 1053-a) on the ground that such a trial would subject him to double jeopardy because he had previously been found not guilty on a charge of reckless driving (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 1190) arising out of the same accident incident, the petition should be dismissed.

 

362 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Goodman v. Del-Sa-Co Foods, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 191; 205 N.E.2d 288; 257 N.Y.S.2d 142; 1965 N.Y. LEXIS 1580


January 6, 1965, Argued  
February 11, 1965, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified and matter remitted to Special Term for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein, with costs to appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent lienor filed an action against appellant owner to enforce a mechanic's lien. The trial court voided the lien because it had been willfully exaggerated. The trial court did not award any civil penalty for willful exaggeration to the owner under N.Y. Lien. Law. § 39-a because the owner did not request such relief. The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) affirmed, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court voided the mechanic's lien because it was willfully exaggerated to some extent, but it made no finding to show what items were willfully exaggerated or by how much. The owner argued that N.Y. Lien. Law 39-a entitled it to an automatic recovery of the entire amount of the discrepancy between the amount of the lien as filed and the amount found due. The court disagreed with the owner's approach and concluded that the intent of the legislature was to provide a civil penalty for only the amount of the wilful exaggeration. The court pointed out that the owner, as the party aggrieved by the lien, had the burden to prove the amount of the wilful exaggeration. The court then noted that the trial court's findings indicated that the lien contained willful exaggeration but that the exact number of items willfully exaggerated and the extent of the exaggeration was not determined nor was any request for such findings made. The court determined that the trial court's finding of willful exaggeration entitled the owner to a civil penalty but that additional findings of fact as to the amount and extent of the exaggeration were necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court to make findings on the evidence or on new evidence to be taken to establish the extent of the civil penalty owed to the owner.


HEADNOTES

Liens -- mechanic's lien -- willful exaggeration of lien -- statutory provision (Lien Law, § 39-a) that owner or contractor recover civil penalty when lien is declared void for willful exaggeration (§ 39) was intended to allow only recovery of amount of such willful exaggeration and not necessarily of entire difference between amount of lien as filed and sum actually due lienor; statute, if held to impose penalty measured by discrepancy due to honest mistake, might be unconstitutional; trial court found existence but not extent of willful exaggeration and Court of Appeals lacks power to make new findings of fact thereon, so matter is remanded to trial court to make findings.

1. Section 39-a of the Lien Law provides that an owner or contractor may recover damages when a mechanic's lien is declared void for willful exaggeration (§ 39), and that such damages "shall include * * * an amount equal to the difference by which the amount claimed to be due or to become due as stated in the notice of lien exceeded the amount actually due or to become due thereon." Such literal language is to be read in conjunction with the immediately preceding sentence in section 39-a providing for recovery only where "the court shall have declared said lien to be void on account of wilful exaggeration" in which event "the person filing such notice of lien shall be liable in damages to the owner or contractor." The draftsman of the statute evidently had chiefly in mind the situation where the entire amount of the exaggeration was willful, and the Legislature intended to allow recovery of this civil penalty only in the amount by which the lien was thus exaggerated. An owner is not entitled to recover anything on account of an honest mistake. Accordingly, when a mechanic's lien filed in the amount of $ 22,804.68 was declared void on the grounds that the amount actually due was but $ 9,380.89 and that there had been some willful exaggeration, but the extent thereof was not determined, automatic recovery of the penalty in the amount of the entire $ 13,423.79 discrepancy cannot be had.

2. If section 39-a were held to impose a penalty measured by a discrepancy due to honest mistake, it might well be unconstitutional.

3. Although the answer did not ask for any affirmative relief, except attorneys' fees incurred in obtaining discharge of the lien, such failure to demand this statutory civil penalty should be overlooked inasmuch as the issue was litigated of whether the lien was willfully exaggerated by some amount.

4. The Court of Appeals lacks power to make new findings of fact on conflicting evidence which could have been made by the trial court or the Appellate Division by determining how much of the discrepancy found was willful. In the absence at the trial court of a request for, or the making of, findings as to the amount of the willful exaggeration, the case should be remanded to the trial court to make the findings.

Crilley v. Allstate Ins. Co.

365 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Eck v. United Arab Airlines, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 53; 203 N.E.2d 640; 255 N.Y.S.2d 249; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 786; 6 A.L.R.3d 1260


October 12, 1964, Argued  
December 3, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order of Appellate Division reversed and that of the Supreme Court, New York County, reinstated, with costs in this court and in the Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger sought review of the order of the Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department, which dismissed her negligence complaint against defendant foreign airline for lack of jurisdiction under article 28 of the Warsaw Convention.


OVERVIEW: The passenger, a California resident, was injured when the foreign airline's plane crashed in Sudan. The passenger brought a negligence action against the foreign airline in New York City because the foreign airline maintained a ticket office in New York City. The trial court denied the foreign airline's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction pursuant to article 28 of the Warsaw Convention. The foreign airline appealed. The appellate division reversed the order and dismissed the complaint. The passenger appealed. The court reversed the order of the appellate division because, under article 28 of the Warsaw Convention, the foreign airline had a place of business in New York City in its ticket office.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- jurisdiction -- Warsaw Convention -- action by plaintiff, California resident, to recover for injuries sustained in crash in Sudan of airplane operated between Jerusalem and Cairo by defendant, foreign airline, will lie in courts of New York where defendant maintained place of business, ticket office, although plaintiff arranged for passage on defendant's plane with Oakland, California, office of another airline -- provision in Warsaw Convention that such action must be brought in territory of one of high contracting parties, either before court of carrier's domicile or of his principal place of business, or where he has place of business through which contract was made, or before court at place of destination, when interpreted to effectuate obvious purpose of contracting powers, did not exclude suit in particular area if carrier had office there and ticket had been purchased in that area or in another part of territory of high contracting party.

The provision in the Warsaw Convention (art. 28) that an action for damages must be brought, at the plaintiff's option, "in the territory of one of the High Contracting Parties, either before the court of the domicile of the carrier or of his principal place of business, or where he has a place of business through which the contract has been made, or before the court at the place of destination" was apparently intended to limit bringing suits to only those forums where the terms of the Convention were in force and would be applied. Moreover, the intent was to avoid suits in countries where the carrier had no office for the making of transportation contracts and where no passage on the carriers' aircraft had been purchased. However, the carriers cannot, by changing their ticket routing methods, deprive purchasers of tickets in a territory of a high contracting party, where the carrier has an office, of access to courts in that jurisdiction as that would conflict with the basic intent that the remedy for passengers similarly situated was to remain constant. Accordingly, an action will lie in the courts of New York against defendant, a foreign airline which maintains a place of business -- a ticket office -- in New York City, although plaintiff, a California resident, arranged for her air passage to several countries in Europe with the Oakland, California, office of another foreign airline which, in turn, obtained for her a ticket on defendant's flight from Jerusalem to Cairo in the course of which she was injured when the aircraft crashed while attempting a nonscheduled stop in the Sudan. When the defendant opened its United States office in New York, it anticipated that it would be amenable to suits there for claims arising out of any carriage sold by that office, and the chance circumstance of where the plaintiff made her purchase of the ticket within this territory of a high contracting party should not relieve the defendant airline of the burden of litigation here when it expects to defend suits on similar contracts originating in its New York office. An authorized venue is provided when there is a place of business in the territory and the sale of a ticket is closed within the territory. Such an application of the treaty parallels its express provisions and does not contradict them.

 

366 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pugach


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


15 N.Y.2d 65; 204 N.E.2d 176; 255 N.Y.S.2d 833; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 787


October 12, 1964, Submitted  
December 3, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted defendant permission to appeal an order of the Appellate Division, First Department (New York), which affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to suppress and convicting him of carrying a concealed weapon in violation N.Y. Penal Law § 1897.


OVERVIEW: While investigating another matter, police officers took defendant into a squad car, spoke to him about the other matter, and frisked him. The frisk led to the discovery of a loaded firearm concealed in defendant's brief case. At trial, defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence obtained from his briefcase. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. On appeal, defendant argued that, absent a showing of the "other matter," no probable cause existed for an arrest, absent which the search of his brief case was illegal and the fruits thereof unavailable as evidence against him. Defendant further argued that the officers' actions during the frisk were unreasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court affirmed, holding that disclosure of the "other matter" was unnecessary in light of proof that defendant and others had been under surveillance for months and that, under all the circumstances, the inclusion of the brief case in the "frisk" was not so unreasonable as to be constitutionally illegal. The court noted that the gun was "concealed" under § 1897. The court found it unnecessary to consider whether the arrest prior to the search of the brief case was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order affirming defendant's conviction of carrying a concealed weapon.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- examination of defendant's brief case as part of "frisk" was not unreasonable and constitutionally illegal.

1. The New York City Police Department had been investigating defendant as to his complicity and connection with "another matter". Two police officers asked defendant to accompany them and, with an officer on either side, he was escorted to a parked squad car where they were joined by a third officer. One officer entered the rear seat of the squad car followed by the defendant and another officer. The third officer entered the front seat at the right of the driver. The officers seated on either side of defendant in the rear seat proceeded to "frisk" the defendant. Defendant put a brief case which he had been holding on his lap on the car floor between his feet. The officers completed the "frisk" after which defendant picked up the brief case and placed it on his lap. One of the officers then took the brief case and examined it and found a gun in it. The finding of the gun resulted from a permissible "frisk" and not from an unreasonable search. Under all the circumstances the inclusion of the brief case in the "frisk" was not so unreasonable as to be constitutionally illegal.

2. For purposes of the trial on the charge of carrying a concealed weapon, the disclosure of the "other matter" was unnecessary in light of proof that the defendant and four others had been under surveillance for several months; that a police officer had fraternized with the defendant for the purpose of procuring information as to his complicity and participation in the "other matter" and that he was, in fact, being taken to a police station for further questioning.

368 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ogden v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 349; 200 N.E.2d 559; 251 N.Y.S.2d 661; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 983


June 10, 1964, Submitted  
July 10, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state education commissioner (commissioner) and city school district, sought review of a decision by the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which annulled and held void the commissioner's determination to consolidate the common school district with the city school district. The action was brought by respondents, the trustees of the common school district, and a voter and taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner sought to consolidate the city school district and the common school district. The commissioner easily obtained the city school district's consent to the consolidation. However, the common school district's consent was obtained only after several meetings. The commissioner entered his consolidation order immediately after obtaining the common school district's consent. The common school district subsequently rescinded its consent. However, the commissioner refused to recognize the rescission and proceeded with the consolidation. Appellees brought an action to have the consolidation order declared null and void. The trial court refused appellees' request. The appellate court reversed, holding that the common school district was entitled to rescind its consent to consolidation. Appellants sought review, and the court affirmed. The court agreed that under N.Y. Educ. Law § 2021(14), the common school district was entitled to repeal its prior decision. Further, the court said, the commissioner acted arbitrarily as a matter of law when he effectively ignored the common school district's right to rescind and ordered consolidation. Thus, the court held the order void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that annulled and held void the commissioner's determination to consolidate the city school district and the common school district after the common school district had rescinded its consent to consolidation.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- consolidation -- State Commissioner of Education acted arbitrarily as matter of law in refusing to withdraw consolidation order which he had issued following vote of common school district and city school district to consolidate, but at time when he had information that special meeting would be held to exercise common school district power to rescind consolidation (cf. Education Law, § 2021, subd. 14) and where common school district rescinded its consent before order of consolidation became effective.

Pursuant to section 1524 of the Education Law, at a school district meeting of Common School District No. 18, a motion was adopted favoring consolidation of this district and the City School District of the City of Middletown. Thereafter, the Board of Education of the Middletown School District adopted a resolution consenting to the consolidation. On June 25, 1963, at a time when he had information that a special meeting was to be held in an effort to exercise the district's power to rescind the consolidation, the State Commissioner of Education issued an order of consolidation effective July 1, 1963. On June 28, 1963 School District No. 18 rescinded its previous action in favor of consolidation. Subdivision 14 of section 2021 of the Education Law provides that, at a school district meeting duly assembled, those entitled to vote shall have power by a majority of those present and voting "To alter, repeal and modify their proceedings, from time to time, as occasion may require." The State Commissioner of Education acted arbitrarily, as a matter of law, in refusing to withdraw his consolidation order when the district meeting had rescinded its action before the Commissioner's order became effective.

 

369 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Larkin v. G. P. Putnam's Sons


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 399; 200 N.E.2d 760; 252 N.Y.S.2d 71; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 991


April 1, 1964, Argued  
July 10, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation counsel and plaintiff district attorneys filed action, pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Code § 22-a, seeking an injunction restraining defendant publisher from selling and distributing a novel. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On review, the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) entered an order that reversed the dismissal and granted the injunction. The publisher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The publisher attempted to sell and distribute a book about a prostitute's exploits written circa 1749. The corporation counsel and the attorneys general for the city filed their complaint seeking to restrain the publisher's actions. On review of the trial court's dismissal of the complaint on the merits, the appellate division found the book came within the proscription of § 22-a. On further review, the court held injunctive relief was not appropriate because § 22-a no longer afforded a constitutionally sound basis for the suppression of a book of the type issued by the publisher.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate division's order that granted the request for an injunction by the corporation and the attorneys general and dismissed the complaint against the publisher, without costs.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- obscene book -- injunction will not issue to restrain selling and distributing book entitled "Memoirs of a Woman of Pleasure", known as "Fanny Hill", under section 22-a of Code of Criminal Procedure, which provides for restraining, selling and distributing book which is "obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent or disgusting" -- book falls within area of permissible publications.

Under section 22-a of the Code of Criminal Procedure, an injunction may issue to restrain the selling and distributing of a book which is "obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent or disgusting". Under the applicable decisions interpreting the constitutional provisions guaranteeing freedom of the press, the book "Memoirs of a Woman of Pleasure", popularly known as "Fanny Hill", may not be suppressed. The book falls within the area of permissible publications.

 

370 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bookcase, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 409; 201 N.E.2d 14; 252 N.Y.S.2d 433; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 992


March 31, 1964, Argued  
July 10, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and the information dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Appellate Term of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed a judgment of the criminal court convicting defendants of the crime of unlawful sale of obscene prints to a minor, under N.Y. Penal Law § 484-h.


OVERVIEW: Defendants attacked the constitutionality of § 484-h, claiming that it abridged freedom of speech and of the press in violation of the First and Fourteenth Amendments because it was too vague for a criminal statute. The court found that the question of constitutionality hinged upon its application to minors under 18 years of age. The court found that the statute made no distinction that it was addressed to minors under 18 years of age. Defendants had not been convicted of selling an obscene book to a minor, but one that was principally devoted to descriptions of illicit sex or sexual immorality, unrelated to whether the book was obscene. The court found that the statute was drawn so broadly as to render criminal sales or other exhibition to the young of pictures and publications of all kinds that were principally devoted to these subjects, in however serious or dignified a manner. The statute was so broad and so obscure in its coverage as to abridge the constitutionally protected freedom of speech and of the press as well as the due process clauses in the federal and state constitutions. Thus, the court reversed the convictions and dismissed the information.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction were reversed and the information dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sale of book to minor -- section 484-h of Penal Law which prohibits sale to minor under 18 years of age of "any book * * * the cover or content of which exploits, is devoted to, or is principally made up of descriptions of illicit sex or sexual immorality" is in violation of First and Fourteenth Amendments to United States Constitution.

Section 484-h of the Penal Law prohibits the sale to a minor under 18 years of age of "any book * * * the cover or content of which exploits, is devoted to, or is principally made up of descriptions of illicit sex or sexual immorality". The statute is in violation of the First Amendment and the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution by denying due process of law in that the language is too vague for a criminal statute and it abridges freedom of speech and the press. Accordingly, the judgment convicting defendants under that statute for the sale to a minor under 18 years of age of a copy of a book entitled "Memoirs of a Woman of Pleasure" ("Fanny Hill") should be reversed and the information dismissed.

 

371 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Paterson v. University of State of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 432; 201 N.E.2d 27; 252 N.Y.S.2d 452; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 994


June 1, 1964, Argued  
July 10, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicants brought an action against defendants, university and others, seeking a declaration that N.Y. Educ. Law art. 148 was unconstitutional and an injunction to restrain defendants from carrying out the statute's provisions. The Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York) dismissed the complaint. The applicants appealed from the order of the Supreme Court, Appellate Division (New York) that affirmed the supreme court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The applicants practiced landscape architecture and were denied a license under the "grandfather clause" in N.Y. Educ. Law § 7323(3). They contended that the statute constituted an invalid exercise of the state's police power and an improper delegation of legislative power. The court affirmed the appellate court's order that affirmed the supreme court's dismissal of the applicants' complaint, as the regulation of landscape architects was a valid exercise of state police power and the statute did not improperly delegate legislative power. The court found that the regulation and practice of landscape architecture were clearly related to the public health and welfare. The court concluded that the legislature could properly give a board of examiners discretion in determining what constituted the "substantial equivalent" of a doctoral degree, as well as to determine what constituted "satisfactory supervised experience," in passing upon the applicants' qualifications for professional preferment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the appellate court that affirmed the supreme court's dismissal of the applicants' action against the university and others.


HEADNOTES

Licenses -- landscape architects -- article 148 of Education Law, providing for licensing of landscape architects, is not unconstitutional -- testimony established that regulation of practice of landscape architecture, profession, was related to public health and welfare and constituted valid exercise of police power -- sections 7320 and 7326 of Education Law, read together, establish sufficiently clear standard of conduct to give notice of what is permitted and what is not -- no improper delegation of legislative power.

1. Article 148 of the Education Law provides for the licensing of landscape architects, prohibits the unlicensed practice of landscape architecture after July 1, 1961, establishes a Board of Examiners to carry out the licensing provisions of the statute, prescribes penal sanctions for the violations of said statutes, and defines the practice of landscape architecture. It also provides that the article shall not be construed to affect or prevent the practice of engineering and other listed occupations, and that no persons shall use the designations landscape architect, landscape architectural or landscape architecture unless licensed under the provisions of the article. The testimony at the trial established that the regulation of practice of landscape architecture, a profession in this State, was clearly related to public health and welfare and, as such, constituted a valid exercise of the police power. The article is not unconstitutional.

2. Although the language of section 7320 of the Education Law, defining the activities of one engaged in landscape architecture, standing alone and without more, might be regarded as too general, when it is read together with section 7326 which explicitly states that the article shall not be construed to prevent practice by licensed engineers, architects and other licensees, and also exempts from its operation a long list of designated occupations and activities, a sufficiently clear standard of conduct is set forth to give fair notice to one concerned with or engaged in the activities regulated as to what acts are criminal and those that are innocent.

3. The statute does not constitute an improper delegation of legislative power. Board of Examiners are the usual and ordinary bodies to pass on the qualifications for professions and the board is properly given some discretion in satisfying itself as to the sufficiency of the grade and character of an applicant.

Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 927; 200 N.E.2d 866; 252 N.Y.S.2d 326; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 1021

373 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wasmuth v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 391; 200 N.E.2d 756; 252 N.Y.S.2d 65; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 990


June 9, 1964, Argued  
July 10, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractors appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an order of the trial court granting a motion to dismiss by defendant Commissioner of Education of the State of New York (commissioner). The chiropractors filed the action, challenging N.Y. Educ. Law art. 132 as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted article 132, which added new requirements for the obtaining a chiropractic license, such as an examination in basic subjects and proficiency in the use of an X ray machine. The chiropractors filed a class action, alleging that the statute created unconstitutional distinctions as between groups of chiropractors and between chiropractors and other groups licensed to practice in the field of human health. The trial court granted the commissioner's motion to dismiss and on appeal, the appellate court and the court affirmed. The court found that article 132 was a valid exercise of the police power in furtherance of the public health. The court determined that because X rays related the chiropractic field, it was neither unreasonable nor inappropriate to require applicants to demonstrate a proficiency in that area. The court determined that the imposition of new requirements for the continued practice of a profession previously carried on without the need of such requirements did not violate the constitution. The court noted that grandfather clauses were common incidents of licensing and a reasonable basis on which to exempt experienced chiropractors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the appellate court, which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the chiropractors' claim.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- practice of chiropractic -- article 132 of Education Law, enacted for licensing of practice of chiropractic, is not unconstitutional -- no denial of equal protection of law -- provisions requiring examination in use and effect of X ray not violative of equal protection clause -- requirements of examination in basic subjects within area of police power -- Legislature could excuse some, under grandfather clause, and not others from passing basic subject test.

1. Article 132 of the Education Law (L. 1963, chs. 780-781, eff. July 1, 1963) enacted for the licensing of the practice of chiropractic in New York State is not unconstitutional. In enacting these provisions there was no denial of the equal protection of the law.

2. The need to regulate and confine the use of X ray to qualified personnel has already been upheld in Chiropractic Assn. of N. Y. v. Hilleboe (12 N Y 2d 109). Since the use of X ray relates to a field where chiropractors will be practicing, it is neither unreasonable nor inappropriate to require chiropractic license applicants to demonstrate a proficiency in that area. The provisions requiring an examination in the use and effect of X ray are not violative of the equal protection clause.

3. The requirements of the statute for examination in the basic subjects pursuant to section 6552 of the Education Law do not render the statute unconstitutional. The practice of chiropractic is connected with human health and within the area of the State's police power.

4. The Legislature could excuse, under a grandfather clause, some and not others from passing the basic subject test.

5. The statute has conferred on chiropractors privileges which they could not claim as a matter of constitutional right, and this in itself meets the challenge that the statute is unconstitutional.

 

374 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Laverne


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 304; 200 N.E.2d 441; 251 N.Y.S.2d 452; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 1047


March 26, 1964, Argued  
June 10, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Nassau County Court (New York), which affirmed a judgment of the lower court, which convicted defendant of violating the Building Zone Ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating the Building Zone Ordinance. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, and defendant sought review. The court held that entry into private premises by a public officer without a search warrant against the resistance of the occupant and in pursuance of the authority of law for the purpose of eliminating a hazard immediately dangerous to health and public safety was constitutionally valid if the purpose was for a summary or another administrative correction. However, the court determined that the public officer illegally searched defendant's apartment without his consent and absent exigent circumstances. The court found that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 813-d had not authorized the suppression of oral testimony and literally addressed only physical evidence. The court reversed the judgments of the lower courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgments of the lower courts, which convicted defendant of violating the Building Zone Ordinance.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- where injunction had been issued against carrying on unlawful business in residential zone and, pursuant to village ordinance, village Building Inspector entered premises and made observations which were basis of criminal prosecution against defendant for violations of ordinance, convictions were result of unlawful search -- convictions reversed and informations dismissed.

A village ordinance authorized the village Building Inspector to "enter any building or premises at any reasonable hour" in discharging his duty to "enforce the provisions of" the Village Building Zone Ordinance and provided that a violation constituted disorderly conduct with a prescribed punishment. An injunction had been issued against the corporation, of which defendant was president, from carrying on the business or professional activity in which he was engaged -- designing furniture, fabrics, wall coverings and similar materials -- in an area zoned for residential use. On three occasions the village Building Inspector entered the premises and made observations after he got in, and these observations were the basis of three criminal prosecutions against defendant for violations of the ordinance. The convictions were the result of an unlawful search of defendant's home, and the judgment affirming the convictions is reversed and the informations dismissed.

In re Estate of Garfield


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 251; 200 N.E.2d 196; 251 N.Y.S.2d 7; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 1075


March 31, 1964, Argued  
June 4, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, with costs in this court and in the Appellate Division, and the matter remitted to the Surrogates' Court for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein. Question certified answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent executrix sought review of the decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an order of a surrogate's court that vacated the executrix' demand for a jury trial in a proceeding for a compulsory accounting in connection with petitioner lawyers' claim against the estate.


OVERVIEW: After the husband of the executrix died, a law firm of lawyers filed a claim against the estate for legal professional services claimed to have been rendered to the husband during his lifetime. The executrix rejected the claim and, almost six years later, the lawyers sought a compulsory accounting. The executrix, in response to the lawyers' petition, filed an affidavit in which she advised the surrogate's court that there were no claims pending against the estate other than the lawyers' claim and that she objected to an accounting. A copy of the affidavit served on the lawyers noted a demand for trial by jury. The lawyers orally moved to vacate the demand for a jury trial on the ground that the executrix was not entitled to a jury trial as a matter of right. The surrogate held that the executrix had no right to a jury trial even as a matter of discretion and accordingly vacated the jury demand. The appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the lawyers' claim was an action at law for work, labor, and services, and that the right to trial by jury in all such cases was preserved by U.S. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the executrix' request for a jury trial in the action for compulsory accounting to settle the lawyers' claim for legal fees because the claim made was an action at law to which a jury trial was guaranteed by the Constitution.


HEADNOTES

Executors and administrators -- claim against estate -- jury trial -- executrix had right to trial by jury of claim made by firm of lawyers for fees and disbursements for legal services allegedly rendered testator -- claim is at law for work, labor and services, and right to trial by jury is preserved by Constitution ( Matter of Boyle, 242 N. Y. 342, distinguished) -- executrix did not waive right to jury trial -- moreover, argument that there was waiver was not made before Surrogate.

1. Sometime after testatrix rejected a claim made by a firm of lawyers for fees and disbursements for legal professional services claimed to have been rendered to testator during his lifetime, claimants filed a petition for a compulsory accounting by the executrix. The executrix filed an affidavit in which she stated that there was no necessity for an accounting other than this claim, and that she was willing to agree to a trial of the claim provided "all of my defenses against the claim and my other rights, both substantive and procedural, in relation thereto are preserved." About two months later she served a duplicate copy of the affidavit and, for the first time, noted thereon that she demanded a trial by jury. The Surrogate stated that he would deem the affidavit to be the executrix' answer. The executrix had a right to a trial by jury and it should not have been denied.

2. Petitioners' claim is at law for work, labor and services, and the right to trial by jury in all such cases is preserved by the Constitution (art. I, § 2; Matter of Boyle, 242 N. Y. 342, distinguished).

3. The executrix did not waive the right to a jury trial. Section 67 of the Surrogate's Court Act provides that a right to trial by jury as to any issue of fact shall be deemed waived unless demanded in writing and served with the answer or objections. The affidavit filed by executrix in opposition to the petitioners' motion for a compulsory accounting was not an "answer" or "objections". The executrix was not asserting any issue of fact on the merits of the claimants' purported legal services but was requesting, rather, that whatever issue might arise should be tried without burdening the estate with the expenses of an accounting. Moreover, the argument that there was a waiver was not made before the Surrogate, and was asserted for the first time in the Appellate Division, which properly disregarded it.

 

376 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Department of Bldgs.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


14 N.Y.2d 291; 200 N.E.2d 432; 251 N.Y.S.2d 441; 1964 N.Y. LEXIS 1079


March 24, 1964, Argued  
June 4, 1964, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review, on constitutional grounds, of an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an order designating respondent Department of Buildings of the City of New York's Commissioner of Real Estate (department) as receiver of the rents, issues and profits of certain premises pursuant to N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 309.


OVERVIEW: The department, acting under the authority of the Receivership Law, petitioned for and obtained an order from the Supreme Court designating the Commissioner of Real Estate as receiver of the rents, issues, and profits of certain premises. The appellate court affirmed and the owner of the premises appealed, urging that the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 309, prompted by the existence of an emergency of truly awesome proportions, was directed to a legitimate objective, and the measures taken were reasonably and appropriately adapted to attain that objective. The court upheld the statute as a valid exercise of the police power, and because there was no departure from § 309 requirements, the order appealed from was affirmed with costs. The court held that the 1962 amendatory act fully remedied any procedural deficiencies. The court also determined that the owner had an opportunity to participate in the proceedings from beginning to end.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the supreme court's decision that affirmed an order designating the Commissioner of Real Estate as receiver of rents, issues, and profits of certain premises.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- dangerously deteriorated multiple dwellings -- city's Commissioner of Real Estate may, after notices and hearing, be appointed receiver of dangerously deteriorated multiple dwelling, for purpose of removing conditions constituting nuisance and danger to occupants or to occupants of adjacent properties or to public (Multiple Dwelling Law, § 309, as amd. by L. 1962, ch. 492) -- 1962 amendments obviate defects which had caused invalidity of 1937 amendment as to mortgagees.

1. A multiple dwelling having become so deteriorated that a nuisance exists therein which endangers life, health or safety, and notices to remove such nuisance having been served on the owner and the mortgagee, and a full hearing having been afforded thereon to the owner and the mortgagee, Special Term of the Supreme Court properly appointed the Commissioner of Real Estate of the City of New York as the receiver of the rents, issues and profits of the premises, for the purpose of removing or remedying the conditions constituting such nuisance (Multiple Dwelling Law, § 309, as amd. by L. 1962, ch. 492).

2. The Legislature found (L. 1962, ch. 492, § 1) that, in the cities to which the Multiple Dwelling Law applies, (a) there are deteriorated or deteriorating multiple dwellings containing conditions which constitute a nuisance and a threat to life, health or safety of their occupants or the occupants of adjacent properties or the general public, and (b) there is a shortage, constituting a public emergency, of safe and habitable dwelling units. The statute (Multiple Dwelling Law, § 309) is reasonably and appropriately adapted to remedy these emergency conditions and is a valid exercise of the police power, even though the effect may be to impair the obligation of the mortgagee's contract with the mortgagor.

3. The statute's detailed provisions for notices and hearings afford due process of law to the owners and mortgagees.

4. The amendments (L. 1962, ch. 492) to section 309 of the Multiple Dwelling Law completely obviate the deficiencies which had caused the Court of Appeals in 1938 to adjudge that a subdivision which had been enacted in 1937 was unconstitutional as to mortgagees (cf. Central Sav. Bank v. City of New York, 279 N. Y. 266, 280 N. Y. 9, cert. den. 306 U.S. 661).
